\t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/states\"\n27: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/tfdiags\"\n28: )\n29: \n30: // PlanOpts are the various options that affect the details of how Terraform\n31: // will build a plan.\n32: type PlanOpts struct {\n33: \t// Mode defines what variety of plan the caller wishes to create.\n34: \t// Refer to the documentation of the plans.Mode type and its values\n35: \t// for more information.\n36: \tMode plans.Mode\n37: \n38: \t// SkipRefresh specifies to trust that the current values for managed\n39: \t// resource instances in the prior state are accurate and to therefore\n40: \t// disable the usual step of fetching updated values for each resource\n41: \t// instance using its corresponding provider.\n42: \tSkipRefresh bool\n43: \n44: \t// PreDestroyRefresh indicated that this is being passed to a plan used to\n45: \t// refresh the state immediately before a destroy plan.\n46: \t// FIXME: This is a temporary fix to allow the pre-destroy refresh to\n47: \t// succeed. The refreshing operation during destroy must be a special case,\n48: \t// which can allow for missing instances in the state, and avoid blocking\n49: \t// on failing condition tests. The destroy plan itself should be\n50: \t// responsible for this special case of refreshing, and the separate\n51: \t// pre-destroy plan removed entirely.\n52: \tPreDestroyRefresh bool\n53: \n54: \t// SetVariables are the raw values for root module variables as provided\n55: \t// by the user who is requesting the run, prior to any normalization or\n56: \t// substitution of defaults. See the documentation for the InputValue\n57: \t// type for more information on how to correctly populate this.\n58: \tSetVariables InputValues\n59: \n60: \t// If Targets has a non-zero length then it activates targeted planning\n61: \t// mode, where Terraform will take actions only for resource instances\n62: \t// mentioned in this set and any other objects those resource instances\n63: \t// depend on.\n64: \t//\n65: \t// Targeted planning mode is intended for exceptional use only,\n66: \t// and so populating this field will cause Terraform to generate extra\n67: \t// warnings as part of the planning result.\n68: \tTargets []addrs.Targetable\n69: \n70: \t// ForceReplace is a set of resource instance addresses whose corresponding\n71: \t// objects should be forced planned for replacement if the provider's\n72: \t// plan would otherwise have been to either update the object in-place or\n73: \t// to take no action on it at all.\n74: \t//\n75: \t// A typical use of this argument is to ask Terraform to replace an object\n76: \t// which the user has determined is somehow degraded (via information from\n77: \t// outside of Terraform), thereby hopefully replacing it with a\n78: \t// fully-functional new object.\n79: \tForceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n80: \n81: \t// DeferralAllowed specifies that the plan is allowed to defer some actions,\n82: \t// so that a subset of the plan can be applied even if parts of it can't yet\n83: \t// be planned at all. Plans that contain deferred actions can't converge in\n84: \t// a single run, and their configuration must be planned again after the\n85: \t// dependencies of their deferred objects are in a usable state. Various\n86: \t// events can cause deferrals, including unknown values in count and\n87: \t// for_each arguments, and deferral notices from providers. If\n88: \t// DeferralAllowed is false, the plan will error upon encountering an object\n89: \t// that would be unplannable until after the apply.\n90: \tDeferralAllowed bool\n91: \n92: \t// ExternalReferences allows the external caller to pass in references to\n93: \t// nodes that should not be pruned even if they are not referenced within\n94: \t// the actual graph.\n95: \tExternalReferences []*addrs.Reference\n96: \n97: \t// ExternalDependencyDeferred, when set, indicates that the caller\n98: \t// considers this configuration to depend on some other configuration\n99: \t// that had at least one deferred change, and therefore everything in\n100: \t// this configuration must have its changes deferred too so that the\n101: \t// overall dependency ordering would be correct.\n102: \tExternalDependencyDeferred bool\n103: \n104: \t// Overrides provides a set of override objects that should be applied\n105: \t// during this plan.\n106: \tOverrides *mocking.Overrides\n107: \n108: \t// GenerateConfigPath tells Terraform where to write any generated\n109: \t// configuration for any ImportTargets that do not have configuration\n110: \t// already.\n111: \t//\n112: \t// If empty, then no config will be generated.\n113: \tGenerateConfigPath string\n114: \n115: \t// ExternalProviders are clients for pre-configured providers that are\n116: \t// treated as being passed into the root module from the caller. This\n117: \t// is equivalent to writing a \"providers\" argument inside a \"module\"\n118: \t// block in the Terraform language, but for the root module the caller\n119: \t// is written in Go rather than the Terraform language.\n120: \t//\n121: \t// Terraform Core will NOT call ValidateProviderConfig or ConfigureProvider\n122: \t// on any providers in this map; it's the caller's responsibility to\n123: \t// configure these providers based on information outside the scope of\n124: \t// the root module.\n125: \tExternalProviders map[addrs.RootProviderConfig]providers.Interface\n126: \n127: \t// ForcePlanTimestamp, if not nil, will force the \"plantimestamp\" function\n128: \t// to return the given value instead of the time when the plan operation\n129: \t// started.\n130: \t//\n131: \t// This is here only to allow producing fixed results for tests. Don't\n132: \t// use it for main code.\n133: \tForcePlanTimestamp *time.Time\n134: \n135: \t// Forget if set to true will cause the plan to forget all resources. This is\n136: \t// only allowd in the context of a destroy plan.\n137: \tForget bool\n138: }\n139: \n140: // Plan generates an execution plan by comparing the given configuration\n141: // with the given previous run state.\n142: //\n143: // The given planning options allow control of various other details of the\n144: // planning process that are not represented directly in the configuration.\n145: // You can use terraform.DefaultPlanOpts to generate a normal plan with no\n146: // special options.\n147: //\n148: // If the returned diagnostics contains no errors then the returned plan is\n149: // applyable, although Terraform cannot guarantee that applying it will fully\n150: // succeed. If the returned diagnostics contains errors but this method\n151: // still returns a non-nil Plan then the plan describes the subset of actions\n152: // planned so far, which is not safe to apply but could potentially be used\n153: // by the UI layer to give extra context to support understanding of the\n154: // returned error messages.\n155: func (c *Context) Plan(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*plans.Plan, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n156: \tplan, _, diags := c.PlanAndEval(config, prevRunState, opts)\n157: \treturn plan, diags\n158: }\n159: \n160: // PlanAndEval is like [Context.Plan] except that it additionally makes a\n161: // best effort to return a [lang.Scope] which can evaluate expressions in the\n162: // root module based on the content of the generated plan.\n163: //\n164: // The scope will be nil if the planning process doesn't complete successfully\n165: // enough to produce a valid evaluation scope. If the returned plan is nil\n166: // then the scope will always be nil, but it's also possible for the scope\n167: // to be nil even when the plan isn't, if the plan is not complete enough for\n168: // the evaluation scope to produce consistent results.\n169: func (c *Context) PlanAndEval(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*plans.Plan, *lang.Scope, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n170: \tdefer c.acquireRun(\"plan\")()\n171: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n172: \n173: \t// Save the downstream functions from needing to deal with these broken situations.\n174: \t// No real callers should rely on these, but we have a bunch of old and\n175: \t// sloppy tests that don't always populate arguments properly.\n176: \tif config == nil {\n177: }\n423: \n424: func (c *Context) refreshOnlyPlan(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*plans.Plan, *lang.Scope, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n425: \tvar diags This is required because\n479: \t// a \"destroy plan\" is only creating delete changes, and is essentially a\n480: \t// local operation.\n481: \t//\n482: \t// NOTE: if skipRefresh _is_ set then we'll rely on the destroy-plan walk\n483: \t// below to upgrade the prevRunState and priorState both to the latest\n484: \t// resource type schemas, so NodePlanDestroyableResourceInstance.Execute\n485: \t// must coordinate with this by taking that action only when c.skipRefresh\n486: \t// _is_ set. This coupling between the two is unfortunate but necessary\n487: \t// to work within our current structure.\n488: \tif !opts.SkipRefresh && !prevRunState.Empty() {\n489: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] Context.destroyPlan: calling Context.plan to get the effect of refreshing the prior state\")\n490: \t\trefreshOpts := *opts\n491: \t\trefreshOpts.Mode = plans.NormalMode\n492: \t\trefreshOpts.PreDestroyRefresh = true\n493: \n494: \t\t// FIXME: A normal plan is required here to refresh the state, because\n495: \t\t// the state and configuration may not match during a destroy, and a\n496: \t\t// normal refresh plan can fail with evaluation errors. In the future\n497: \t\t// the destroy plan should take care of refreshing instances itself,\n498: \t\t// where the special cases of evaluation and skipping condition checks\n499: \t\t// can be done.\n500: \t\trefreshPlan, _, refreshDiags := c.plan(config, prevRunState, &refreshOpts)\n501: \t\tif refreshDiags.HasErrors() {\n502: \t\t\t// NOTE: Normally we'd append diagnostics regardless of whether\n503: \t\t\t// there are errors, just in case there are warnings we'd want to\n504: \t\t\t// preserve, but we're intentionally _not_ doing that here because\n505: \t\t\t// if the first plan does mean we won't show any warnings that would've been\n509: \t\t\t// unique to only this walk, but we're assuming here that if the\n510: \t\t\t// warnings aren't also applicable to a destroy plan then we'd\n511: \t\t\t// rather not show them here, because this non-destroy plan for\n512: \t\t\t// refreshing is largely an implementation detail.)\n513: \t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(refreshDiags)\n514: \t\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n515: \t\t}\n516: \n517: \t\t// We'll use the refreshed state -- which is the  \"prior state\" from\n518: \t\t// the perspective of this \tdestroyPlan, evalScope, walkDiags := c.planWalk(config, priorState, opts)\n531: \tdiags = diags.Append(walkDiags)\n532: \tif walkDiags.HasErrors() {\n533: \t\t// Non-nil plan along with errors diags\n537: \t}\n538: \n539: \tif !opts.SkipRefresh {\n540: \t\t// If we didn't skip refreshing then we want the previous run state to\n541: \t\t// be the one we originally fed into the diags\n551: }\n552: \n553: func (c *Context) prePlanFindAndApplyMoves(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State) ([]refactoring.MoveStatement, refactoring.MoveResults, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n554: \texplicitMoveStmts := refactoring.FindMoveStatements(config)\n555: \timplicitMoveStmts := refactoring.ImpliedMoveStatements(config, prevRunState, explicitMoveStmts)\n556: \tvar moveStmts []addrs.Targetable) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n567: \tif len(targets) < 1 {\n568: \t\treturn nil // the following only matters when targeting\n569: \t}\n570: \n571: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n572: \n573: \tvar excluded []addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n574: \tfor _, result := range moveResults.Changes.Values() {\n575: \t\tfromMatchesTarget := false\n576: \t\ttoMatchesTarget := false\n577: \t\tfor _, targetAddr := range targets {\n578: \t\t\tif targetAddr.TargetContains(result.From) {\n579: \t\t\t\tfromMatchesTarget = true\n580: \t\t\t}\n581: \t\t\tif targetAddr.TargetContains(result.To) {\n582: \t\t\t\ttoMatchesTarget = true\n583: \t\t\t}\n584: \t\t}\n585: \t\tif !fromMatchesTarget {\n586: \t\t\texcluded = append(excluded, result.From)\n587: \t\t}\n588: \t\tif !toMatchesTarget {\n589: \t\t\texcluded = append(excluded, result.To)\n590: \t\t}\n591: \t}\n592: \tif len(excluded) > 0 {\n593: \t\tsort.Slice(excluded, func(i, j int) bool {\n594: \t\t\treturn excluded[i].Less(excluded[j])\n595: \t\t})\n596: \n597: \t\tvar listBuf strings.Builder\n598: \t\tvar prevResourceAddr addrs.AbsResource\n599: \t\tfor _, instAddr := range excluded {\n600: \t\t\t// Targeting generally ends up selecting whole resources rather\n601: \t\t\t// than individual instances, because we don't factor in\n602: \t\t\t// individual instances until DynamicExpand, so we're going to\n603: \t\t\t// always show whole resource addresses here, excluding any\n604: \t\t\t// instance keys. (This also neatly avoids dealing with the\n605: \t\t\t// different quoting styles required for string instance keys\n606: \t\t\t// on different shells, which is handy.)\n607: \t\t\t//\n608: \t\t\t// To avoid showing duplicates when we have multiple instances\n609: \t\t\t// of the same resource, we'll remember the most recent\n610: \t\t\t// resource we rendered in prevResource, which is sufficient\n611: \t\t\t// because we sorted the list of instance addresses above, and\n612: \t\t\t// our sort order always groups together instances of the same\n613: \t\t\t// resource.\n614: \t\t\tresourceAddr := instAddr.ContainingResource()\n615: \t\t\tif resourceAddr.Equal(prevResourceAddr) {\n616: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n617: \t\t\t}\n618: \t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&listBuf, \"\\n  -target=%q\", resourceAddr.String())\n619: \t\t\tprevResourceAddr = resourceAddr\n620: \t\t}\n621: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n622: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n623: \t\t\t\"Moved resource instances excluded by targeting\",\n624: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n625: \t\t\t\t\"Resource instances in your current state have moved to new addresses in the latest configuration. Terraform must include those resource instances while planning in order to ensure a correct result, but your -target=... options do not fully cover all of those resource instances.\\n\\nTo create a valid plan, either remove your -target=... options altogether or add the following additional target options:%s\\n\\nNote that adding these options may include further additional resource instances in your plan, in order to respect object dependencies.\",\n626: \t\t\t\tlistBuf.String(),\n627: \t\t\t),\n628: \t\t))\n629: \t}\n630: \n631: \treturn diags\n632: }\n633: \n634: func (c *Context) postPlanValidateMoves(config *configs.Config, stmts []refactoring.MoveStatement, allInsts instances.Set) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n635: \treturn refactoring.ValidateMoves(stmts, config, allInsts)\n636: }\n637: \n638: // findImportTargets builds a list of import targets from any import blocks in\n639: // config.\n640: func (c *Context) findImportTargets(config *configs.Config) []*ImportTarget {\n641: (c *Context) findForgetTargets(config *configs.Config) (forgetResources []addrs.ConfigResource, forgetModules []addrs.Module, diags tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n653: \tremoveStmts, diags := \t\t}\n669: \t}\n670: \treturn forgetResources, forgetModules, diags\n671: }\n672: \n673: func (c *Context) planWalk(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*plans.Plan, *lang.Scope, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n674: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n675: \tlog.Printf(\"[DEBUG] Building and walking plan graph for %s\", opts.Mode)\n676: \n677: \tprevRunState = prevRunState.DeepCopy() // don't modify the caller's object when we process the moves\n678: \tmoveStmts, moveResults, moveDiags := c.prePlanFindAndApplyMoves(config, prevRunState)\n679: \tdiags = \t\texternalProviderConfigs = opts.ExternalProviders\n709: \t}\n710: \n711: \t// If we get here then we should definitely have a non-nil \"graph\", which\n712: \t// we can now walk.\n713: \tchanges := This oddity\n742: \t\t// comes from the fact that we need to apply the moves before we\n743: \t\t// actually validate them, because validation depends on the result\n744: \t\t// of first trying to plan.\n745: \t\treturn nil, nil, moveValidateDiags\n746: \t}\n747: \tdiags = diags.Append(moveValidateDiags) // might just contain warnings\n748: \n749: \tif moveResults.Blocked.Len() > 0 && !diags.HasErrors() {\n750: \t\t// If we had blocked moves and we're not going to be returning errors\n751: \t\t// then we'll report the blockers as a warning.        states.NewCheckResults(walker.Checks),\n811: \t\tTimestamp:               timestamp,\n812: \t\tProviderFunctionResults: providerFuncResults.GetHashes(),\n813: \n814: \t\t// Other fields get populated by Context.Plan after we return\n815: \t}\n816: \n817: \t// Our final rulings on whether the plan is \"complete\" and \"applyable\".\n818: \t// See the documentation for these plan fields to targets or deferred actions should be\n823: \t\t\t// complete if we didn't encounter errors while producing it.\n824: \t\t\tlog.Println(\"[TRACE] Plan is complete\")\n825: \t\t\tplan.Complete = true\n826: \t\t} else {\n827: \t\t\tlog.Println(\"[TRACE] Plan is incomplete\")\n828: \t\t}\n829: \t\tif opts.Mode == plans.RefreshOnlyMode {\n830: \t\t\t// In refresh-only mode we explicitly don't expect to propose any\n831: \t\t\t// actions, but the plan is applyable if the state was changed\n832: \t\t\t// in an interesting way by the refresh step.\n833: \t\t\tplan.Applyable = !plan.PriorState.ManagedResourcesEqual(plan.PrevRunState) || !plan.PriorState.RootOutputValuesEqual(plan.PrevRunState)\n834: \t\t} else {\n835: \t\t\t// For other planning modes a plan is applyable if its \"changes\"\n836: \t\t\t// are not considered empty (by whatever rules the plans package\n837: \t\t\t// uses to decide that).\n838: \t\t\tplan.Applyable = !plan.Changes.Empty()\n839: \t\t}\n840: \t\tif plan.Applyable {\n841: \t\t\tlog.Println(\"[TRACE] Plan is applyable\")\n842: \t\t} else {\n843: \t\t\tlog.Println(\"[TRACE] Plan is not applyable\")\n844: \t\t}\n845: \t} else {\n846: \t\tlog.Println(\"[WARN] Planning encountered errors, so plan is not applyable\")\n847: \t}\n848: \n849: \t// The caller also gets access to an expression evaluation scope in the\n850: \t// root addrs.RootModuleInstance)\n853: \n854: \treturn plan, evalScope, diags\n855: }\n856: \n857: func (c *Context) deferredResources(config *configs.Config, deferrals *PlanOpts) (*Graph, walkOperation, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n888: \tvar externalProviderConfigs map[addrs.RootProviderConfig]providers.Interface\n889: \tif opts != nil {\n890: driftedResources is a best-effort attempt to compare the current and prior\n955: // state. If we cannot decode the prior state for some reason, this should only\n956: // return warnings to help the user correlate any missing resources in the\n957: // report. This is known to happen when targeting a subset of resources,\n958: // because the excluded instances will have been removed from the plan and\n959: // not upgraded.\n960: func (c *Context) driftedResources(config *configs.Config, oldState, newState *states.State, moves refactoring.MoveResults) ([]*plans.ResourceInstanceChangeSrc, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n961: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n962: \n963: \tif newState.ManagedResourcesEqual(oldState) && moves.Changes.Len() == 0 {\n964: \t\t// Nothing to do, because we only detect and report drift for managed\n965: \t\t// resource instances.\n966: \t\treturn nil, diags\n967: \t}\n968: \n969: \tschemas, schemaDiags := c.Schemas(config, newState)\n970: \tdiags = diags.Append(schemaDiags)\n971: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n972: \t\treturn nil, diags\n973: \t}\n974: \n975: \tvar drs []*plans.ResourceInstanceChangeSrc\n976: \n977: \tfor _, ms := range oldState.Modules {\n978: \t\tfor _, rs := range ms.Resources {\n979: \t\t\tif rs.Addr.Resource.Mode != addrs.ManagedResourceMode {\n980: \t\t\t\t// Drift reporting is only for managed resources\n981: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n982: \t\t\t}\n983: \n984: \t\t\tprovider := rs.ProviderConfig.Provider\n985: \t\t\tfor key, oldIS := range rs.Instances {\n986: \t\t\t\tif oldIS.Current == nil {\n987: \t\t\t\t\t// Not interested in instances that only have deposed objects\n988: \t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n989: \t\t\t\t}\n990: \t\t\t\taddr := rs.Addr.Instance(key)\n991: \n992: \t\t\t\t// Previous run address defaults to the current address, but\n993: \t\t\t\t// can differ if the resource moved before refreshing\n994: \t\t\t\tprevRunAddr := addr\n995: \t\t\t\tif move, ok := moves.Changes.GetOk(addr); ok {\n996: \t\t\t\t\tprevRunAddr = move.From\n997: \t\t\t\t}\n998: \n999: \t\t\t\tnewIS := newState.ResourceInstance(addr)\n1000: \n1001: \t\t\t\tschema, _ := schemas.ResourceTypeConfig(\n1002: \t\t\t\t\tprovider,\n1003: \t\t\t\t\taddr.Resource.Resource.Mode,\n1004: \t\t\t\t\taddr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n1005: \t\t\t\t)\n1006: \t\t\t\tif schema == nil {\n1007: \t\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n1008: \t\t\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Warning,\n1009: \t\t\t\t\t\t\"Missing resource schema from provider\",\n1010: \t\t\t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"No resource schema found for %s when decoding prior state\", addr.Resource.Resource.Type),\n1011: \t\t\t\t\t))\n1012: \t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n1013: \t\t\t\t}\n1014: \t\t\t\tty := schema.ImpliedType()\n1015: \n1016: \t\t\t\toldObj, err := oldIS.Current.Decode(ty)\n1017: \t\t\t\tif err != nil {\n1018: \t\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n1019: \t\t\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Warning,\n1020: \t\t\t\t\t\t\"Failed to decode resource from state\",\n1021: \t\t\t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"Error decoding %q from prior state: %s\", addr.String(), err),\n1022: \t\t\t\t\t))\n1023: \t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n1024: \t\t\t\t}\n1025: \n1026: \t\t\t\tvar newObj *states.ResourceInstanceObject\n1027: \t\t\t\tif newIS != nil && newIS.Current != nil {\n1028: \t\t\t\t\tnewObj, err = newIS.Current.Decode(ty)\n1029: \t\t\t\t\tif err != nil {\n1030: \t\t\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n1031: \t\t\t\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Warning,\n1032: \t\t\t\t\t\t\t\"Failed to decode resource from state\",\n1033: \t\t\t\t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"Error decoding %q from prior state: %s\", addr.String(), err),\n1034: \t\t\t\t\t\t))\n1035: \t\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n1036: \t\t\t\t\t}\n1037: \t\t\t\t}\n1038: \n1039: \t\t\t\tvar oldVal, newVal cty.Value\n1040: \t\t\t\toldVal = oldObj.Value\n1041: \t\t\t\tif newObj != nil {\n1042: \t\t\t\t\tnewVal = newObj.Value\n1043: \t\t\t\t} else {\n1044: \t\t\t\t\tnewVal = cty.NullVal(ty)\n1045: \t\t\t\t}\n1046: \n1047: \t\t\t\tif oldVal.RawEquals(newVal) && addr.Equal(prevRunAddr) {\n1048: \t\t\t\t\t// No drift if the two values are semantically equivalent\n1049: \t\t\t\t\t// and no move has happened\n1050: \t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n1051: \t\t\t\t}\n1052: \n1053: \t\t\t\t// We can detect three types of changes after refreshing state,\n1054: \t\t\t\t// only two of which are easily understood as \"drift\":\n1055: \t\t\t\t//\n1056: \t\t\t\t// - Resources which were deleted outside of Terraform;\n1057: \t\t\t\t// - Resources where the object value has changed outside of\n1058: \t\t\t\t//   Terraform;\n1059: \t\t\t\t// - Resources which have been moved without other changes.\n1060: \t\t\t\t//\n1061: \t\t\t\t// All of these are returned as drift, to allow refresh-only plans\n1062: \t\t\t\t// to present a full set of changes which will be applied.\n1063: \t\t\t\tvar action plans.Action\n1064: \t\t\t\tswitch {\n1065: \t\t\t\tcase newVal.IsNull():\n1066: \t\t\t\t\taction = plans.Delete\n1067: \t\t\t\tcase !oldVal.RawEquals(newVal):\n1068: \t\t\t\t\taction = plans.Update\n1069: \t\t\t\tdefault:\n1070: \t\t\t\t\taction = plans.NoOp\n1071: \t\t\t\t}\n1072: \n1073: \t\t\t\tchange := &plans.ResourceInstanceChange{\n1074: \t\t\t\t\tAddr:         addr,\n1075: \t\t\t\t\tPrevRunAddr:  prevRunAddr,\n1076: \t\t\t\t\tProviderAddr: rs.ProviderConfig,\n1077: \t\t\t\t\tChange: plans.Change{\n1078: \t\t\t\t\t\tAction: action,\n1079: \t\t\t\t\t\tBefore: oldVal,\n1080: \t\t\t\t\t\tAfter:  newVal,\n1081: \t\t\t\t\t},\n1082: \t\t\t\t}\n1083: \n1084: \t\t\t\tchangeSrc, err := change.Encode(ty)\n1085: \t\t\t\tif err != nil {\n1086: \t\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(err)\n1087: \t\t\t\t\treturn nil, diags\n1088: \t\t\t\t}\n1089: \n1090: \t\t\t\tdrs = append(drs, changeSrc)\n1091: \t\t\t}\n1092: \t\t}\n1093: \t}\n1094: \n1095: \treturn drs, diags\n1096: }\n1097: \n1098: // PlanGraphForUI is a last vestage of graphs in the public interface of Context\n1099: // (as opposed to graphs as an implementation detail) intended only for use\n1100: // by the \"terraform graph\" command when asked to render a plan-time graph.\n1101: //\n1102: // The result of this is intended only for rendering to the user as a dot\n1103: // graph, and so may change in future in order to make the result more useful\n1104: // in that context, even if drifts away Makes its decisions primarily based on the given configuration, which\n25: //     represents the desired state.\n26: //\n27: //   - Ignores certain lifecycle concerns like create_before_destroy, because\n28: //     those are only important once we already know what action we're planning\n29: //     to take against a particular resource instance.\n30: type PlanGraphBuilder struct {\n31: \t// Config is the configuration tree to build a plan from.\n32: \tConfig *configs.Config\n33: \n34: \t// State is the current state\n35: \tState *states.State\n36: \n37: \t// RootVariableValues are the raw input values for root input variables\n38: \t// given by the caller, which we'll resolve into final values as part\n39: \t// of the plan walk.\n40: \tRootVariableValues InputValues\n41: \n42: \t// ExternalProviderConfigs are pre-initialized root module provider\n43: \t// configurations that the graph builder should assume will be available\n44: \t// immediately during the subsequent plan walk, without any explicit\n45: \t// initialization step.\n46: \tExternalProviderConfigs map[addrs.RootProviderConfig]providers.Interface\n47: \n48: \t// Plugins is a library of plug-in components (providers and\n49: \t// provisioners) available for use.\n50: \tPlugins *contextPlugins\n51: \n52: \t// Targets are resources to target\n53: \tTargets []addrs.Targetable\n54: \n55: \t// ForceReplace are resource instances where if we would normally have\n56: \t// generated a NoOp or Update action then we'll force generating a replace\n57: \t// action instead. Create and Delete actions are not affected.\n58: \tForceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n59: \n60: \t// skipRefresh indicates that we should skip refreshing managed resources\n61: \tskipRefresh bool\n62: \n63: \t// preDestroyRefresh indicates that we are executing the refresh which\n64: \t// happens immediately before a destroy plan, which happens to use the\n65: \t// normal planing mode so skipPlanChanges cannot be set.\n66: \tpreDestroyRefresh bool\n67: \n68: \t// skipPlanChanges indicates that we should skip the step of comparing\n69: \t// prior state with configuration and generating planned changes to\n70: \t// resource instances. (This is for the \"refresh only\" planning mode,\n71: \t// where we _only_ do the refresh step.)\n72: \tskipPlanChanges bool\n73: \n74: \tConcreteProvider                ConcreteProviderNodeFunc\n75: \tConcreteResource                ConcreteResourceNodeFunc\n76: \tConcreteResourceInstance        ConcreteResourceInstanceNodeFunc\n77: \tConcreteResourceOrphan          ConcreteResourceInstanceNodeFunc\n78: \tConcreteResourceInstanceDeposed ConcreteResourceInstanceDeposedNodeFunc\n79: \tConcreteModule                  ConcreteModuleNodeFunc\n80: \n81: \t// Plan Operation this graph will be used for.\n82: \tOperation walkOperation\n83: \n84: \t// ExternalReferences allows the external caller to pass in references to\n85: \t// nodes that should not be pruned even if they are not referenced within\n86: \t// the actual graph.\n87: \tExternalReferences []*addrs.Reference\n88: \n89: \t// Overrides provides the set of overrides supplied by the testing\n90: \t// framework.\n91: \tOverrides *mocking.Overrides\n92: \n93: \t// ImportTargets are the list of resources to import.\n94: \tImportTargets []*ImportTarget\n95: \n96: \t// forgetResources lists the resources that are to be forgotten, i.e. removed\n97: \t// from state without destroying.\n98: \tforgetResources []addrs.ConfigResource\n99: \n100: \t// forgetModules lists the modules that are to be forgotten, i.e. removed\n101: \t// from state without destroying.\n102: \tforgetModules []addrs.Module\n103: \n104: \t// GenerateConfig tells Terraform where to write and generated config for\n105: \t// any import targets that do not already have configuration.\n106: \t//\n107: \t// If empty, then config will not be generated.\n108: \tGenerateConfigPath string\n109: }\n110: \n111: // See GraphBuilder\n112: func (b *PlanGraphBuilder) Build(path addrs.ModuleInstance) (*Graph, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n113: \tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] building graph for %s\", b.Operation)\n114: \treturn (&BasicGraphBuilder{\n115: \t\tSteps: b.Steps(),\n116: \t\tName:  \"PlanGraphBuilder\",\n117: \t}).Build(path)\n118: }\n119: \n120: // See GraphBuilder\n121: func (b *PlanGraphBuilder) Steps() []GraphTransformer {\n122: \tswitch b.Operation {\n123: \tcase walkPlan:\n124: \t\tb.initPlan()\n125: \tcase walkPlanDestroy:\n126: \t\tb.initDestroy()\n127: \tcase walkValidate:\n128: (During plan this will\n195: \t\t// intentionally skip creating nodes for _current_ objects, since\n196: \t\t// ConfigTransformer created nodes that will do that during\n197: \t\t// DynamicExpand.)\n198: \t\t&StateTransformer{\n199: \t\t\tConcreteCurrent: b.ConcreteResourceInstance,\n200: \t\t\tConcreteDeposed: b.ConcreteResourceInstanceDeposed,\n201: \t\t\tState:           b.State,\n202: \t\t},\n203: \n204: \t\t// Attach the state\n205: \t\t&AttachStateTransformer{State: b.State},\n206: \n207: \t\t// Create orphan output nodes\n208: \t\t&OrphanOutputTransformer{\n209: \t\t\tConfig:   b.Config,\n210: \t\t\tState:    b.State,\n211: \t\t\tPlanning: true,\n212: \t\t},\n213: \n214: \t\t// Attach the configuration to any resources\n215: \t\t&AttachResourceConfigTransformer{Config: b.Config},\n216: \n217: \t\t// add providers\n218: \t\ttransformProviders(b.ConcreteProvider, b.Config, b.ExternalProviderConfigs),\n219: \n220: \t\t// Remove modules no longer present in the config\n221: \t\t&RemovedModuleTransformer{Config: b.Config, State: b.State},\n222: \n223: \t\t// Must attach schemas before ReferenceTransformer so that we can\n224: \t\t// analyze the configuration to find references.\n225: \t\t&AttachSchemaTransformer{Plugins: b.Plugins, Config: b.Config},\n226: \n227: \t\t// Create expansion nodes for all of the module calls. This must\n228: \t\t// come after all other transformers that create nodes representing\n229: \t\t// objects that can belong to modules.\n230: \t\t&ModuleExpansionTransformer{Concrete: b.ConcreteModule, Config: b.Config},\n231: \n232: \t\t// Plug in any external references.\n233: \t\t&ExternalReferenceTransformer{\n234: \t\t\tExternalReferences: b.ExternalReferences,\n235: \t\t},\n236: \n237: \t\t&ReferenceTransformer{},\n238: \n239: \t\t&AttachDependenciesTransformer{},\n240: \n241: \t\t// Make sure data sources are aware of any depends_on from the\n242: \t\t// which nodes to keep in the graph.\n247: \t\t&DestroyEdgeTransformer{\n248: \t\t\tOperation: b.Operation,\n249: \t\t},\n250: \n251: \t\t&pruneUnusedNodesTransformer{\n252: \t\t\tskip: b.Operation != \t\t&ephemeralResourceCloseTransformer{skip: b.Operation == walkValidate},\n264: \n265: \t\t// Close opened plugin connections\n266: \t\t&CloseProviderTransformer{},\n267: \n268: \t\t// Close the root possible).\n273: \t\t&TransitiveReductionTransformer{},\n274: \t}\n275: \n276: \treturn steps\n277: }\n278: \n279: func (b *PlanGraphBuilder) initPlan() {\n280: \tb.ConcreteProvider = func(a Plans that contain deferred actions can't converge in\n84: \t// a single run, and their configuration must be planned again after the\n85: \t// dependencies of their deferred objects are in a usable state. Various\n86: \t// events can cause deferrals, including unknown values in count and\n87: \t// for_each arguments, and deferral notices from providers. dependency graph for a plan is built via `PlanGraphBuilder` in `internal/terraform/graph_builder_plan.go`:\n\n1. **Graph Builder Creation**:\n   - `c.planGraph()` in `context_plan.go:887` creates a mode (lines 135-274):\n\n   a. **ConfigTransformer** (lines 137-146): Creates nodes for all resources in the configuration.\n\n   b. **RootVariableTransformer** & **ModuleVariableTransformer** (lines Gets the current state value\n     2. Calls `provider.ReadResource()` RPC to fetch the current remote state\n     3. Terraform's plan architecture:\n\n### **Q1: Command to Context**\nThe CLI command (`terraform plan`) flows through:\n- `PlanCommand.Run()` → parses arguments\n- `PrepareBackend()` → loads backend\n- `OperationRequest()` → builds operation with PlanOpts (Mode, Targets, ForceReplace, etc.)\n- Backend delegates to `Context.Plan()` which accepts config, state, and PlanOpts\n\n### **Q2: Graph Construction Pipeline**\n`PlanGraphBuilder.Steps()` sequences 25 transformers:\n- **ConfigTransformer** creates resource nodes\n- **ReferenceTransformer** (key stage) analyzes node references and adds
